<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p><i><b>Finding Dory</b></i> is a 2016 American <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer-animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy-drama" title="Comedy-drama">comedy-drama</a> <a href="/wiki/Adventure_film" title="Adventure film">adventure film</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar Animation Studios</a> and released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>. Directed and co-written by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a> with co-direction by <a href="/wiki/Angus_MacLane" title="Angus MacLane">Angus MacLane</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HR1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-HR1-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1-6">[6]</a></sup> the screenplay was written by Victoria Strouse and Stanton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-covered_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-covered-7">[7]</a></sup> The film is a sequel/spinoff<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> to 2003's <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i> and features the returning voices of <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Brooks" title="Albert Brooks">Albert Brooks</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Hayden_Rolence" title="Hayden Rolence">Hayden Rolence</a> (replacing <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gould" title="Alexander Gould">Alexander Gould</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ed_O%27Neill" title="Ed O'Neill">Ed O'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaitlin_Olson" title="Kaitlin Olson">Kaitlin Olson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ty_Burrell" title="Ty Burrell">Ty Burrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diane_Keaton" title="Diane Keaton">Diane Keaton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Levy" title="Eugene Levy">Eugene Levy</a> joining the cast. <i>Finding Dory</i> focuses on the <a href="/wiki/Anterograde_amnesia" title="Anterograde amnesia">amnesiac</a> fish Dory, who journeys to be reunited with her parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dory_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dory-9">[9]</a></sup> Along the way, she is captured and taken to a California <a href="/wiki/Public_aquarium" title="Public aquarium">public aquarium</a>, from which Marlin and Nemo attempt to rescue her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film premiered at the <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on June 8, 2016, and was released in the United States on June 17, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Upon release, the film was a critical and commercial success, grossing over $1 billion worldwide, becoming the first Pixar film to cross this mark since 2010's <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>. The film set numerous records, including the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_animated_films" title="List of highest-grossing openings for animated films">highest-grossing animated film opening of all time in North America</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dory, as a child, gets separated from her parents. As she grows up, Dory attempts to search for them, gradually forgetting them due to her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-term_memory_loss" title="Short-term memory loss">short-term memory loss</a>. After accidentally running in with Marlin, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clownfish" title="Clownfish">clownfish</a>, who's <a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">looking for his missing son</a>, she goes to help him.</p>
<p>One year after reuniting Nemo with Marlin, Dory has become a helping hand in raising Nemo. One day during a <a href="/wiki/Field_trip" title="Field trip">field trip</a> with Nemo's class to learn about migration, Dory recalls through a childhood flashback that she has a family. She decides to look for them but finds her short-term memory loss to be an obstacle. The only thing she remembers is that they lived at the Jewel of <a href="/wiki/Morro_Bay,_California" title="Morro Bay, California">Morro Bay</a>.</p>
<p>Marlin and Nemo accompany Dory in her quest. With the help of Crush, they ride a <a href="/wiki/California_Current" title="California Current">water current</a> to California. Upon arrival, Dory accidentally awakens a predatory <a href="/wiki/Squid" title="Squid">squid</a>, who immediately pursues them, almost devouring Nemo during the chase. Marlin tends to his son afterwards and berates Dory for almost getting him killed. Feeling hurt, Dory travels to the surface to seek help and is captured by staff members from the nearby Marine Life Institute after being caught in <a href="/wiki/Six_pack_rings" title="Six pack rings">six pack rings</a>.</p>
<p>Dory is sent to the quarantine section and tagged. There she meets a grouchy yet well-meaning, seven-legged <a href="/wiki/Octopus" title="Octopus">octopus</a> named Hank. Dory's tag shows that she will be sent to an aquarium in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>. Due to a traumatic ocean life, Hank wants to live in the aquarium instead of being released back into the ocean, so he agrees to help Dory find her parents in exchange for her tag. In one exhibit, Dory encounters her childhood friend Destiny, a nearsighted <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a> who used to communicate with Dory through pipes, and Bailey, a <a href="/wiki/Beluga_whale" title="Beluga whale">beluga whale</a> who believes he has lost his ability to <a href="/wiki/Animal_echolocation" title="Animal echolocation">echolocate</a>. Dory subsequently has <a href="/wiki/Flashback_(psychology)" title="Flashback (psychology)">flashbacks</a> of life with her parents and struggles to recall details, but finally remembers how she was separated from her parents: she overheard her mother crying one night (presumably about Dory's wellbeing), left home to retrieve a shell in hopes of cheering her up, and was pulled away by an undertow current. Subsequently, she learns that the rest of her <a href="/wiki/Paracanthurus" title="Paracanthurus">regal blue tangs</a> species are being moved to Cleveland.</p>
<p>Marlin and Nemo attempt to rescue Dory. With the help of two <a href="/wiki/California_sea_lion" title="California sea lion">sea lions</a> named Fluke and Rudder and a disfigured <a href="/wiki/Common_loon" title="Common loon">common loon</a> named Becky, they manage to get into the institute, and reunite with her in the pipe system. Back in Quarantine, they locate the tank of blue tangs who tell them that Dory's parents escaped the Institute a long time ago to search for Dory but never came back. This leaves Dory under the impression that they died. Hank retrieves Dory from the tank, accidentally leaving Marlin and Nemo behind. He is then apprehended by one of the employees and unintentionally drops Dory into the drain flushing her to the ocean. Whilst wandering aimlessly, she comes across a trail of shells; remembering that when she was young, her parents had set out a similar trail to teach her how to find her way back home, she follows it. At the end of the trail, Dory finds an empty home with multiple shell trails leading away from it. As she turns to leave, she sees her parents Jenny and Charlie in the distance and joyfully reunites with them. They tell her they have spent years forming trails for her to follow in the hopes that she would eventually find them.</p>
<p>Marlin, Nemo, and Hank end up in the truck taking various aquatic life to Cleveland. Destiny and Bailey escape from their exhibit to help Dory rescue them. Once on board the truck, Dory persuades Hank to return to the sea with her, and together, they hijack the <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">truck</a> and drive it down a busy road before crashing it into the water, freeing all the fish. Dory, along with her parents and new friends, return to the reef with Marlin and Nemo.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Post-credits_scene" title="Post-credits scene">post-credits scene</a>, Gerald makes another attempt to get to the rock where Fluke and Rudder are, only to be repelled by them again, while the Tank Gang from the first film, still trapped inside their (now <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>-covered) plastic bags, reach California one year after floating across the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. They are promptly <a href="/wiki/Rescue" title="Rescue">rescued</a> by the staff members from before, with Bloat asking for the second time, "Now what?". Fluke and Rudder, who watched this happen, fall asleep again not noticing that Gerald reached the rock by sneaking and afterwards, he chuckles menacingly.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_cast">Voice cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Voice cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> as Dory, a <a href="/wiki/Paracanthurus" title="Paracanthurus">regal blue tang</a> who suffers from short-term memory loss.
<ul>
<li>Sloane Murray as Baby Dory. Murray is the seven-year-old daughter of producer Lindsey Collins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lucia Geddes as Tween Dory.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Brooks" title="Albert Brooks">Albert Brooks</a> as Marlin, an overprotective <a href="/wiki/Ocellaris_clownfish" title="Ocellaris clownfish">ocellaris clownfish</a>, Nemo's father and Dory's friend.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hayden_Rolence" title="Hayden Rolence">Hayden Rolence</a> as Nemo, a young optimistic clownfish and Marlin's son. In the previous film, he was voiced by Alexander Gould (who also voices Passengers Carl and Tommy).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ed_O%27Neill" title="Ed O'Neill">Ed O'Neill</a> as Hank, a cranky <a href="/wiki/East_Pacific_red_octopus" title="East Pacific red octopus">East Pacific red octopus</a> who previously lost a tentacle.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diane_Keaton" title="Diane Keaton">Diane Keaton</a> as Jenny, Dory's mother.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eugene_Levy" title="Eugene Levy">Eugene Levy</a> as Charlie, Dory's father.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kaitlin_Olson" title="Kaitlin Olson">Kaitlin Olson</a> as Destiny, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myopia" title="Myopia">near-sighted</a> <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a> and Dory's childhood friend.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ty_Burrell" title="Ty Burrell">Ty Burrell</a> as Bailey, a <a href="/wiki/Beluga_whale" title="Beluga whale">beluga whale</a> who temporarily lost <a href="/wiki/Animal_echolocation" title="Animal echolocation">echolocation</a> due to a concussion.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Idris_Elba" title="Idris Elba">Idris Elba</a> as Fluke, a <a href="/wiki/California_sea_lion" title="California sea lion">sea lion</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dominic_West" title="Dominic West">Dominic West</a> as Rudder, a sea lion and Fluke's friend.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Peterson_(filmmaker)" title="Bob Peterson (filmmaker)">Bob Peterson</a> as Mr. Ray, a <a href="/wiki/Spotted_eagle_ray" title="Spotted eagle ray">spotted eagle ray</a> and Nemo's schoolteacher.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a> as Crush, a <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a> that lives on the <a href="/wiki/East_Australian_Current" title="East Australian Current">East Australian Current</a>, and the Seagulls.</li>
<li>Bennett Dammann as Squirt, Crush's son. He was voiced by Nicholas Bird in the previous film.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Hader" title="Bill Hader">Bill Hader</a> as Stan, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kelp_bass" title="Kelp bass">kelp bass</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kate_McKinnon" title="Kate McKinnon">Kate McKinnon</a> as Stan's wife.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a> as herself, the voice intercom announcer for the Institute PA system.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gould" title="Alexander Gould">Alexander Gould</a> as Passenger Carl, a delivery truck driver that works for the Institute, and Passenger Tommy, Carl's co-worker. Gould voiced Nemo in the previous film.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Ratzenberger" title="John Ratzenberger">John Ratzenberger</a> as Bill, a crab.</li>
<li>Torbin Xan Bullock as Gerald, an outcast California sea lion who is frequently treated with hostility by Fluke and Rudder, and Becky, a friendly and helpful but dimwitted <a href="/wiki/Common_loon" title="Common loon">common loon</a>.</li>
<li>Katherine Ringgold as Kathy, a chickenfish.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angus_MacLane" title="Angus MacLane">Angus MacLane</a> as Charlie Back-and-Forth, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oceanic_sunfish" title="Oceanic sunfish">sunfish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Willem_Dafoe" title="Willem Dafoe">Willem Dafoe</a> as Gill, a <a href="/wiki/Moorish_idol" title="Moorish idol">Moorish idol</a>, who is the leader of the "Tank Gang."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brad_Garrett" title="Brad Garrett">Brad Garrett</a> as Bloat, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pufferfish" title="Pufferfish">pufferfish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Allison_Janney" title="Allison Janney">Allison Janney</a> as Peach, a pink <a href="/wiki/Starfish" title="Starfish">starfish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Austin_Pendleton" title="Austin Pendleton">Austin Pendleton</a> as Gurgle, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_gramma" title="Royal gramma">royal gramma</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Root" title="Stephen Root">Stephen Root</a> as Bubbles, a <a href="/wiki/Yellow_tang" title="Yellow tang">yellow tang</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vicki_Lewis" title="Vicki Lewis">Vicki Lewis</a> as Deb/Flo, a <a href="/wiki/Dascyllus_melanurus" title="Dascyllus melanurus">four-striped damselfish</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jerome_Ranft" title="Jerome Ranft">Jerome Ranft</a> as Jacques, a <a href="/wiki/Cleaner_shrimp" title="Cleaner shrimp">cleaner shrimp</a>. He was voiced by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ranft" title="Joe Ranft">Joe Ranft</a>, Jerome's late brother, in the previous film.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prior to work on <i>Finding Dory</i>, Disney had planned to make a <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i> sequel without Pixar's involvement, through <a href="/wiki/Circle_7_Animation" title="Circle 7 Animation">Circle 7 Animation</a>, a studio Disney announced in 2005 with the intention to make sequels to Pixar properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> However, in 2006, Circle 7 was shut down by Disney without ever having produced a film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Stanton.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="972" data-file-width="1080" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Andrew_Stanton.jpg/220px-Andrew_Stanton.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Andrew_Stanton.jpg/330px-Andrew_Stanton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Andrew_Stanton.jpg/440px-Andrew_Stanton.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Stanton.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Director Andrew Stanton at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Annecy_International_Animated_Film_Festival" title="Annecy International Animated Film Festival">Annecy International Animated Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2012, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a> was developing a sequel to <i>Finding Nemo</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sequel_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-sequel-16">[16]</a></sup> with Victoria Strouse writing the script and a release date scheduled for 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN2_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FN2-17">[17]</a></sup> However, the same day the news of a potential sequel broke, Stanton posted a message on his personal Twitter calling into question the accuracy of these reports. The message said, "Didn't you all learn from <i><a href="/wiki/Chicken_Little_(2005_film)" title="Chicken Little (2005 film)">Chicken Little</a></i>? Everyone calm down. Don't believe everything you read. Nothing to see here now. #skyisnotfalling."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> According to a report by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> published in August 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> was in negotiations to reprise her role of Dory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In September 2012, it was confirmed by Stanton, saying: "What was immediately on the list was writing a second <i><a href="/wiki/John_Carter_(film)" title="John Carter (film)">Carter</a></i> movie. When that went away, everything slid up. I know I'll be accused by more sarcastic people that it's a reaction to <i>Carter</i> not doing well, but only in its timing, but not in its conceit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In February 2013, it was confirmed by the press that <a href="/wiki/Albert_Brooks" title="Albert Brooks">Albert Brooks</a> would reprise the role of Marlin in the sequel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2013, Disney announced the sequel, <i>Finding Dory</i>, for November 25, 2015, confirming that DeGeneres and Brooks would be reprising their roles as Dory and Marlin, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THRDory2015_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-THRDory2015-22">[22]</a></sup> Following a long campaign for a sequel on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i>, DeGeneres stated:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I have waited for this day for a long, long, long, long, long, long time. I'm not mad it took this long. I know the people at Pixar were busy creating <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">Toy Story</a> 16</i>. But the time they took was worth it. The script is fantastic. And it has everything I loved about the first one: It's got a lot of heart, it's really funny, and the best part is—it's got a lot more Dory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THRDory2015_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-THRDory2015-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In a July 2013 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, Stanton spoke of the sequel's origin: "There was polite inquiry from Disney [about a <i>Finding Nemo</i> sequel]. I was always 'No sequels, no sequels.' But I had to get on board from a <a href="/wiki/Vice_president" title="Vice president">VP</a> standpoint. [Sequels] are part of the necessity of our staying afloat, but we don't want to have to go there for those reasons. We want to go there creatively, so we said [to Disney], 'Can you give us the timeline about when we release them? Because we'd like to release something we actually want to make, and we might not come up with it the year you want it.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2016 interview Stanton stated how the film's story came to be; "I don't watch my films that often after they're done because I have to watch them so many times before they come out. So about 2010 when we were getting <i>Finding Nemo</i> ready for the 10-year re-release in 3D, it was interesting to watch again after all that time. Something kind of got lodged in the back of my brain and started to sort of stew. I started to think about how easily Dory could get lost and not find Marlin and Nemo again. She basically was in the same state that she was when Marlin found her. I didn't know where she was from. I knew that she had spent most of her youth wandering the ocean alone, and I wanted to know that she could find her new family, if she ever got lost again. It's almost like the parental side of me was worried." Stanton additionally stated: "I knew if I ever said <i>Finding Dory</i> or mentioned a sequel to <i>Finding Nemo</i> out loud, I’d be done, [T]here would be no way I'd be able to put that horse back in the barn. So I kept it very quiet until I knew I had a story that I thought would hold, and that was in early 2012. So I pitched it to <a href="/wiki/John_Lasseter" title="John Lasseter">John Lasseter</a> and he was all into it. Then I got a writer, and once we had a treatment that we kind of liked, I felt comfortable calling Ellen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Stanton selected Victoria Strouse to write the screenplay. She later said, "It was always collaborative with Andrew, but really the screenwriting was me. Of course, Andrew would do passes, and he and I would brainstorm a lot together and then we would bring it to the group of story artists. People would weigh in and share ideas."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKittrick_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-McKittrick-25">[25]</a></sup> She pointed to Dory's forgetfulness as a challenge when writing the script, adding, "You don't realize until you sit down to write a character who can't remember things how integral memory is to absolutely everything we do, and that's what creates a narrative that people can follow. When a main character can't self-reflect and can't tell a story, that character is very difficult to design because she can't really lead. To get her to be able to lead and to get an audience to be able to trust her was the hardest thing to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKittrick_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-McKittrick-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fictional Marine Life Institute depicted extensively in the film is based on the production team's research trips to the <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Bay_Aquarium" title="Monterey Bay Aquarium">Monterey Bay Aquarium</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Marine_Mammal_Center" title="The Marine Mammal Center">the Marine Mammal Center</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Aquarium" title="Vancouver Aquarium">Vancouver Aquarium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagan_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eagan-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film's ending was revised after Pixar executives viewed <i><a href="/wiki/Blackfish_(film)" title="Blackfish (film)">Blackfish</a></i>, a 2013 documentary film which focuses on the dangers of keeping <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" title="Killer whale">orca whales</a> in captivity. Initially, some of the characters were to end up in a <a href="/wiki/SeaWorld" title="SeaWorld">SeaWorld</a>-like marine park, but the revision gave them an option to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On September 18, 2013, it was announced that the film would be pushed back to a June 17, 2016, release. Pixar's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Dinosaur" title="The Good Dinosaur">The Good Dinosaur</a></i> was moved to the November 25, 2015, release window to allow more time for production of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014, it was revealed through Stanton's <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> feed that the film would be co-directed by <a href="/wiki/Angus_MacLane" title="Angus MacLane">Angus MacLane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slashfilm1_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-slashfilm1-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2015, at Disney's <a href="/wiki/D23_(Disney)#2015" title="D23 (Disney)">D23 Expo</a>, it was announced that Hayden Rolence would voice Nemo, replacing <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gould" title="Alexander Gould">Alexander Gould</a> from the first film, whose voice has deepened since reaching adulthood (Gould voiced a minor character in the sequel instead).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGND232015SequelPlot_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGND232015SequelPlot-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In addition to Rolence, <a href="/wiki/Ed_O%27Neill" title="Ed O'Neill">Ed O'Neill</a> was revealed to be the voice of Hank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGND232015SequelPlot_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-IGND232015SequelPlot-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>To make light more realistic, <a href="/wiki/RenderMan_(software)" title="RenderMan (software)">RenderMan</a> was completely re-engineered, its biggest change in 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>

<p>The film's soundtrack entitled <i>Finding Dory: Original Motion Picture Soundtrack</i> was composed by Thomas Newman and released on June 17, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhaleNewman_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-WhaleNewman-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">Louis Armstrong</a>'s version of "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Wonderful_World" title="What a Wonderful World">What a Wonderful World</a>" is played during the scene in which fish are released into the ocean as the truck Dory and Hank are driving crashes into the water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-licensed-music_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-licensed-music-36">[36]</a></sup> On May 20, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Sia_Furler" title="Sia Furler">Sia</a> performed a cover of <a href="/wiki/Nat_King_Cole" title="Nat King Cole">Nat King Cole's</a> "<a href="/wiki/Unforgettable_(Nat_King_Cole_song)" title="Unforgettable (Nat King Cole song)">Unforgettable</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i> following an announcement that it would be featured in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-licensed-music_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-licensed-music-36">[36]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Finding Dory</i> premiered at the <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on June 8, 2016, and was theatrically released in the United States on June 17, 2016, in 2D, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3-D</a> and <a href="/wiki/RealD_3D" title="RealD 3D">RealD 3D</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HR1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-HR1-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1-6">[6]</a></sup> It was also released to select <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> 3D theaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In April 2016, it was announced that a new Pixar short, <i><a href="/wiki/Piper_(2016_film)" title="Piper (2016 film)">Piper</a></i>, directed by Alan Barillaro and with music by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Belew" title="Adrian Belew">Adrian Belew</a>, would be shown in front of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> It had its UK premiere at the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Film_Festival" title="Edinburgh International Film Festival">Edinburgh International Film Festival</a> on June 18, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film was re-released for Labor Day weekend in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Finding Dory</i> was released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a> on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> (2D and 3D) and <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> in the United States on November 15, 2016, with a <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">digital release</a> on October 25. The DVD release includes the short film, <i><a href="/wiki/Piper_(2016_film)" title="Piper (2016 film)">Piper</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Finding Dory</i> grossed $486.3 million in the U.S. and Canada and $541.8 million in other countries for a worldwide total of $1.028 billion, against a budget of $200 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-4">[4]</a></sup> It had a worldwide opening of $185.7 million, which is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_animated_films" title="List of highest-grossing openings for animated films">second biggest of all time</a> for an animated film behind <i><a href="/wiki/Ice_Age:_Dawn_of_the_Dinosaurs" title="Ice Age: Dawn of the Dinosaurs">Ice Age: Dawn of the Dinosaurs</a></i> ($218.4 million), and an IMAX global opening of $6.4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FORBESopen_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FORBESopen-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup> On August 16, it became the fourth film of 2016 to earn $900 million in ticket sales,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> and on October 9—its seventeenth weekend—it passed the $1 billion threshold, becoming the third film of 2016 to reach that mark joining <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America:_Civil_War" title="Captain America: Civil War">Captain America: Civil War</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Zootopia" title="Zootopia">Zootopia</a></i>, the second Pixar film (after <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>), the fifth animated film (after <i>Toy Story 3</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)">Frozen</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Minions_(film)" title="Minions (film)">Minions</a></i>, and <i>Zootopia</i>), the twelfth Disney film (fourth Disney animated film), and the twenty-seventh film overall in cinematic history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1B_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-1B-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Worldwide, it is the <a href="/wiki/2016_in_film" title="2016 in film">second highest-grossing film of 2016</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldgross_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldgross-49">[49]</a></sup> the highest-grossing animated film of 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldgross_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-worldgross-49">[49]</a></sup> the second highest-grossing Pixar film ever,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pixar_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pixar-50">[50]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_animated_films" title="List of highest-grossing animated films">fourth highest-grossing animated film of all time</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">22nd highest-grossing film of all time</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the United States and Canada, <i>Finding Dory</i> opened on June 17, 2016, alongside <i><a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence" title="Central Intelligence">Central Intelligence</a></i>, with projections having the film grossing $110–120 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fdoweekend_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fdoweekend-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Preview_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Preview-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadproj_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadproj-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> in its opening weekend, with some estimates going as high as $130 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FDOW_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FDOW-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> It received the widest release for a Pixar film (4,305 theaters, breaking <i><a href="/wiki/Brave_(2012_film)" title="Brave (2012 film)">Brave</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s record), of which 3,200 venues were in 3D, along with 425 premium large format locales, approximately 100 IMAX theaters and a handful of <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Cinema" title="Dolby Cinema">Dolby Cinema</a> sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadproj_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deadproj-53">[53]</a></sup> It was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fandango_Media" title="Fandango Media">Fandango</a>'s top pre-selling animated film of all time, outselling the previous record-holder, <i>Minions</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The film grossed $9.2 million from Thursday night previews, a record for both Pixar and any animated film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thursday_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thursday-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and $54.7 million on its opening day, marking both the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_animated_films#Biggest_opening_day_in_U.S._and_Canada_for_an_animated_film_since_1992" title="List of highest-grossing openings for animated films">biggest opening day</a> and single-day for an animated film. This also marks the first time that an animated film has grossed over $50 million in a single day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> It went on to gross $135.1 million in its opening weekend, finishing first at the box office and setting the record for the highest opening weekend for both Pixar (breaking <i>Toy Story 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s record) and any animated film (breaking <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_the_Third" title="Shrek the Third">Shrek the Third</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s record), and became the third biggest adjusted for inflation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> It is also the second highest opening (excluding <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel</a> films and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i>) for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a> behind <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest</a></i> ($135.6 million) and is the studio's eighth biggest debut overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FORBESopen_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-FORBESopen-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> It also became the fifth animated film and the fifth film of 2016 to open above $100 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DEADopen_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-DEADopen-64">[64]</a></sup> Morever, its opening also marked the second biggest for the month of June, behind only <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Its opening was 93.8% above <i>Finding Nemo</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s $70.3 million debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOMopen_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOMopen-66">[66]</a></sup> It further broke the record for the biggest PLF and <a href="/wiki/Cinemark_Theatres" title="Cinemark Theatres">Cinemark XD</a> opening for an animated film with $10.4 million and $2.6 million, respectively. In IMAX, it made $5 million from 211 theaters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup> the third best animated IMAX opening behind <i>Zootopia</i> ($5.2 million) and <i>Toy Story 3</i> ($8.4 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOOM_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOOM-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following its record-breaking openings, it scored the biggest Monday for Pixar by grossing $19.6 million (breaking <i>Toy Story 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s $15.6 million) and the best Monday in June for an animated film. However, among all animated films, it is ranked second — behind 2004's <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">Shrek 2</a></i>, which made $23.4 million on its first Monday,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and it is also the biggest Tuesday for an animated film with $23.2 million, besting <i>Minions</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> $16.8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> It jumped 18.5% over its Monday gross, a rare achievement for a film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It crossed the $200 million mark in its first seven days, becoming the first (and fastest) animated film to pass the said milestone in just a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> It fell only 46% in its <a href="/wiki/Second_weekend_in_box_office_performance" title="Second weekend in box office performance">second weekend</a> earning $73 million to record the biggest second weekend for an animated film (breaking <i>Shrek 2</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s $72.2 million previous record), the biggest for Disney and 2016 (surpassing <i>Captain America: Civil War</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s $72.6 million), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_second_weekends_for_films#Biggest_second_weekends_in_the_U.S._and_Canada" title="List of highest-grossing second weekends for films">eighth biggest second weekend</a> gross of all time overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> This was despite facing stiff competition from newcomer <i><a href="/wiki/Independence_Day:_Resurgence" title="Independence Day: Resurgence">Independence Day: Resurgence</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> It crossed $300 million in 12 days — a new record for an animated film, surpassing the previous record held by <i>Shrek 2</i> and <i>Toy Story 3</i> (both of which took 18 days),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and became the second animated film of 2016 (after <i>Zootopia</i>), the fourth Disney film of 2016, and the sixth overall film of the year to cross the milestone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> It continued to dominate the box office for the third straight weekend, despite competitions from three new wide releases—<i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Tarzan_(film)" title="The Legend of Tarzan (film)">The Legend of Tarzan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Purge:_Election_Year" title="The Purge: Election Year">The Purge: Election Year</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_BFG_(2016_film)" title="The BFG (2016 film)">The BFG</a></i>—after witnessing a 42% decline to $41.8 million in three days and $51.4 million in four days, respectively, during the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">Independence Day</a> holiday frame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DEADopening_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-DEADopening-78">[78]</a></sup> This made it the second time in two years and just the third time since 1992, the July 4th holiday box office was topped by a film in its third weekend of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> It broke another record as it passed the $400 million mark in 21 days, which is the fastest for an animated film, the fastest of 2016, the fastest for the studio, and the fifth fastest of all time overall. Morever, it became the second film of 2016 (after <i>Captain America: Civil War</i>), the fifth animated film, the ninth film for the studio, and the twenty-fourth film overall to pass the milestone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On the following day (July 8), it surpassed <i>Civil War</i> to become the biggest film of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> It dropped out of the top ten in its eighth week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the film was finally overtaken by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_Life_of_Pets" title="The Secret Life of Pets">The Secret Life of Pets</a></i> (and <i>The Legend of Tarzan</i> in second place) in its fourth weekend, it nevertheless passed <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i> to become the highest-grossing Disney animated film of all time in the same weekend, surpassing the latter which held the record for 15 non-consecutive years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In just 30 days, it overtook <i>Shrek 2</i> ($441.2 million) to become the highest-grossing animated film of all time, breaking the latter's record of 12 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VVV_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-VVV-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Four days later, on July 20, it became the first ever animated film in cinematic history to cross the $450 million mark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>As with its predecessor <i>Finding Nemo</i>, the studio expanded the theater count for the film during the <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> weekend from 345 theaters to 2,075 theaters, an addition of 1,730 theaters. In 2003, <i>Nemo</i> was expanded from 838 sites to 1,053 locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>It became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_2016_box_office_number-one_films_in_the_United_States" title="List of 2016 box office number-one films in the United States">second highest-grossing film of 2016</a> (behind <i><a href="/wiki/Rogue_One" title="Rogue One">Rogue One</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> the highest-grossing Pixar film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pixar_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pixar-50">[50]</a></sup> the highest-grossing <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> release, the highest-grossing Disney animated film, the highest-grossing animated film overall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">eighth highest-grossing film of all time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_North_America">Outside North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Outside North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Internationally, <i>Finding Dory</i> received a staggered release in a span of four months from June to September, with Germany being the last country. This was done in order take advantage of key holidays and competitive dates around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas27thOpening_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas27thOpening-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas28thOpening_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas28thOpening-94">[94]</a></sup> It was released across 29 countries—which is 32% of its entire international release territories—the same weekend as its U.S. premiere. It made an estimated $50.7 million to take the No. 1 spot at the international box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup> In its second weekend, it added $38.7 million from 37 markets, falling in third place behind <i>Independence Day: Resurgence</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Now_You_See_Me_2" title="Now You See Me 2">Now You See Me 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas27thOpening_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas27thOpening-93">[93]</a></sup> In the same weekend along with its $73 million take in North America, the film helped Pixar cross the $10 billion mark worldwide since <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">Toy Story</a></i> (1995).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas27thOpening_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas27thOpening-93">[93]</a></sup> By its fourth weekend, the animated film helped Disney push past the $3 billion mark internationally and $5 billion globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>It had the biggest opening for an animated film in Brazil ($7.1 million) and the Netherlands ($2.1 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas28thOpening_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas28thOpening-94">[94]</a></sup> and the biggest of all time for a Disney animated or Pixar film in Australia ($7.7 million), the Philippines ($2.1 million), Singapore ($1.3 million), India ($1 million), Indonesia, Peru and Central America, and in Russia it opened with $3.2 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas28thOpening_94-2"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas28thOpening-94">[94]</a></sup> and the second biggest in the United Kingdom and Ireland ($10.7 million), Mexico ($9.4 million) and Argentina ($3.5 million), and that's despite amidst the latter country's <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica_Centenario" title="Copa América Centenario">Copa America soccer match</a>, and Colombia ($2.1 million), behind <i><a href="/wiki/Monsters_University" title="Monsters University">Monsters University</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas30thOpening_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas30thOpening-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas32ndOpening_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas32ndOpening-98">[98]</a></sup> In the UK and Ireland, the film recorded the second biggest animated opening of the year with £8.1 million ($10.7 million) from 580 theaters, behind only <i>The Secret Life of Pets</i>. However, if previews are excluded, <i>Finding Dory</i> is ahead. Moreover, it also posted the second biggest Disney/Pixar opening, behind only <i>Toy Story 3</i> (fourth biggest if previews are included), and the seventh biggest animated opening of all time overall based on pure Friday-to-Sunday gross alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas32ndOpening_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas32ndOpening-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> It added an additional 43 theaters in its second weekend, after which it added another £3.98 million ($5.1 million) at the weekend, thereby passing the £20 million mark in just 10 days (among Pixar films, only <i>Toy Story 3</i> reached £20 million faster). It made an impressive £8.15 million during weekdays, from Monday to Thursday resulting in a £2.03 million daily average gross. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, this was because of the school holidays that prevailed on the weekdays. Otherwise, family films earn the vast majority of their takings on Saturday and Sunday, and showtimes typically reduce on weekdays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> It returned to the top of the box office in its fourth weekend<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and went on to become the highest-grossing film of the summer this year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In Brazil, in addition to recording the biggest Disney/Pixar opening ever, almost twice the previous record held by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Dinosaur" title="The Good Dinosaur">The Good Dinosaur</a></i>, it also set a new record for an all-time animated opening, on par with <i>Minions</i> in local currency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas28thOpening_94-3"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas28thOpening-94">[94]</a></sup> In South Korea, it had the biggest opening for a Pixar film with $7.1 million, which is also the second biggest for a Disney animated film, behind <i>Frozen</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup> In Japan, the film had a two-day weekend opening of $7 million on Saturday and Sunday from 511 screens on 571,000 admissions. For the entire three-day holiday weekend, including <a href="/wiki/Marine_Day" title="Marine Day">Marine Day</a> on Monday July 18, the film earned $11 million on 922,000 admissions. This made it the top western release of the weekend and the biggest foreign opening weekend in the country so far of this year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas30thOpening_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas30thOpening-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> It had further number-one openings in Spain ($4.9 million), France ($4.7 million), Hong Kong ($1.9 million; $2.8 million including previews), Taiwan ($1.9 million), Sweden, Norway and Denmark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas27thOpening_93-3"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas27thOpening-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas30thOpening_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas30thOpening-97">[97]</a></sup> It topped the box office in the Netherlands for three<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas30thOpening_97-3"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas30thOpening-97">[97]</a></sup> and in Spain and Australia for four consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup> In Italy, it scored the biggest animated opening of the year with $5.8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas40thOpening_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas40thOpening-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>In China, where Pixar films have been struggling to find broad audiences and accrue lucrative revenues, the film was projected to make around $30 million in its opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFIUpstreamStruggle_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-CFIUpstreamStruggle-106">[106]</a></sup> The film ended up grossing $17.7 million—the highest Pixar opening in the country's history—debuting in second place behind <i><a href="/wiki/Warcraft_(film)" title="Warcraft (film)">Warcraft</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas26thOpening_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas26thOpening-45">[45]</a></sup> It surpassed <i>Monsters University</i> in just seven days to become the biggest Pixar film there with $38.1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas28thOpening_94-4"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas28thOpening-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-4"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup> It opened in Germany—its last market—on September 29, where the film delivered a robust opening of $8.4 million, the biggest for any film of 2016 in the country. The film continued to benefit from <a href="/wiki/German_Unity_Day" title="German Unity Day">German Unity Day</a> on October 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas42ndOpening_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas42ndOpening-107">[107]</a></sup> It went on to top the box office there for three straight weekends and even tying with <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(2016_film)" title="Inferno (2016 film)">Inferno</a></i> in its third weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas44thOpening_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas44thOpening-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is now the highest-grossing Disney animated or Pixar film in Australia (where it is also the second highest-grossing animated film of all time behind <i>Shrek 2</i>), Bolivia, Brazil, Central America, Colombia, India, Indonesia, New Zealand, Peru, the Philippines, and Trinidad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas29thOpening_95-5"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas29thOpening-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas30thOpening_97-4"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas30thOpening-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overseas31stOpening_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas31stOpening-109">[109]</a></sup> It also became the second highest-grossing Pixar release of all time in South Korea behind <i><a href="/wiki/Inside_Out_(2015_film)" title="Inside Out (2015 film)">Inside Out</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Elsewhere, the biggest markets in terms of total earnings were Japan ($65.9 million), followed by the UK ($55 million), China ($38.4 million), Australia ($36.2 million) and Brazil ($34.5 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1B_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-1B-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Finding Dory</i> received positive reviews from critics. On <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, the film has an approval rating of 94% based on 268 reviews and an average rating of 7.6/10. The site's critical consensus reads, "Funny, poignant, and thought-provoking, <i>Finding Dory</i> delivers a beautifully animated adventure that adds another entertaining chapter to its predecessor's classic story."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RT_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-RT-111">[111]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, the film has a score of 77 out of 100, based on 48 critics, indicating "generally favorable reviews."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meta_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meta-112">[112]</a></sup> Audiences polled by <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> gave the film an average grade of "A" on an A+ to F scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CinemaScore_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-CinemaScore-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mike Ryan of <i><a href="/wiki/Uproxx" title="Uproxx">Uproxx</a></i> gave the film a positive review, saying: "I never thought I wanted a sequel to <i>Finding Nemo</i>, but here we are and I'm pretty happy it exists. And, for me, it was a more emotional experience than the first film. <i>Finding Dory</i> got me – it made me cry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A.O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> said that while the film lacks "dazzling originality," he overall wrote, "it more than makes up for in warmth, charm and good humor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In his review for <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>, Owen Gleiberman wrote, "It's a film that spills over with laughs (most of them good, a few of them shticky) and tears (all of them earned), supporting characters who are meant to slay us (and mostly do) with their irascible sharp tongues, and dizzyingly extended flights of physical comedy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morgenstern" title="Joe Morgenstern">Joe Morgenstern</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> said that "<i>Finding Dory</i> can be touching, sweet and tender, but it's compulsively, preposterously and steadfastly funny."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> gave the film three-and-a-half stars out of four and said that the film "brims with humor, heart and animation miracles," despite lacking "the fresh surprise of its predecessor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_controversies_and_issues">Environmental controversies and issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Environmental controversies and issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Conservationists warned that very much like <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>, the film could lead to uninformed customers buying <a href="/wiki/Paracanthurus" title="Paracanthurus">blue tangs</a> for home aquariums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Blue tangs cannot be bred in captivity and have to be caught in the wild.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> They are related to <a href="/wiki/Acanthuridae" title="Acanthuridae">surgeonfish</a> and exhibit razor-sharp spines on both sides of the tail that can inflict formidable wounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>While promoting the film, actress <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> reminded audiences that Nemo’s and Dory’s real-life home, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a>, is under enormous threat<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> mostly due to <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a>, a process induced by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, which has killed <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> on an enormous scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">Sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finding_Dory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In June 2016, director <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Stanton" title="Andrew Stanton">Andrew Stanton</a> talked about the possibility of a sequel, saying that he would never exclude it because of the introduction of new characters, citing the <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_(franchise)" title="Toy Story (franchise)">Toy Story</a></i> films as guides for how to expand a world through sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
